      <p><b>Somaliland</b> (<a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a>: <i lang="so">Somaliland</i>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">صوماليلاند</span>‎ <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Ṣūmālīlānd</i></i>, <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic-language text">أرض الصومال</span>‎ <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Arḍ aṣ-Ṣūmāl</i></i>), officially the <b>Republic of Somaliland</b> (<a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a>: <i lang="so">Jamhuuriyadda Soomaaliland</i>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">جمهورية صوماليلاند</span>‎ <i>Jumhūrīyat Ṣūmālīlānd</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">self-declared</a> <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>, internationally considered<sup id="cite_ref-Tukpmorttsep_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tukpmorttsep-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> to be part of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>. The government of Somaliland regards itself as the successor state to <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a>, which, as the briefly independent <a href="/wiki/State_of_Somaliland" title="State of Somaliland">State of Somaliland</a>, united in 1960 with the <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_Somaliland" title="Trust Territory of Somaliland">Trust Territory of Somaliland</a> (the former <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>) to form the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Republic" title="Somali Republic">Somali Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopædia_Britannica_2002_p.835_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopædia_Britannica_2002_p.835-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somaliland lies in the Horn of Africa, on the southern coast of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> to the south and west, and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Its claimed territory has an area of 176,120 square kilometres (68,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-auto_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">[6]</a></sup> with approximately 3.5 million residents in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-7">[7]</a></sup> The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1988, the <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Siad Barre</a> government began a crackdown against the Hargeisa-based <a href="/wiki/Somali_National_Movement" title="Somali National Movement">Somali National Movement</a> (SNM) and other militant groups, which were among the events that led to the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">Somali Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Locsg_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Locsg-14">[14]</a></sup> The conflict left Somalia's economic and military infrastructure severely damaged. Following the collapse of Barre's government in early 1991, local authorities, led by the SNM, <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Somaliland Declaration of Independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> from Somalia on 18 May of the same year and reinstated the borders of the former short-lived independent <a href="/wiki/State_of_Somaliland" title="State of Somaliland">State of Somaliland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-const_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-const-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 1991, the territory has been governed by democratically elected governments that seek international recognition as the government of the Republic of Somaliland.<sup id="cite_ref-profile_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The central government maintains <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Somaliland" title="Foreign relations of Somaliland">informal ties</a> with some foreign governments, who have sent delegations to <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Ethiopia also maintains a <a href="/wiki/Trade_office" title="Trade office">trade office</a> in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> However, Somaliland's self-proclaimed independence has not been officially recognised by any country or international organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Unrepresented_Nations_and_Peoples_Organization" title="Unrepresented Nations and Peoples Organization">Unrepresented Nations and Peoples Organization</a>, an advocacy group whose members consist of indigenous peoples, minorities and unrecognised or occupied territories.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_and_etymology">Name and etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Somalis#Etymology" title="Somalis">Somalis §&nbsp;Etymology</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The name <i>Somaliland</i> is derived from two words: "<a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somali</a>" and "land". The area was named when <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> took control from the <a href="/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt" title="Khedivate of Egypt">Egyptian administration</a> in 1884, after signing successive treaties with the ruling Somali Sultans from the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Issa_(clan)" title="Issa (clan)">Issa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gadabursi" class="mw-redirect" title="Gadabursi">Gadabursi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Warsangali" title="Warsangali">Warsangali</a> clans. The British established a <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> in the region referred to as <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a>. In 1960, when the protectorate became <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(State_of_Somaliland)" title="Independence Day (State of Somaliland)">independent</a> from Great Britain, it was called <a href="/wiki/State_of_Somaliland" title="State of Somaliland">State of Somaliland</a>. Four days later, on 1 July 1960, Somaliland united with <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>. The name "Republic of Somaliland" was taken upon the <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Somaliland Declaration of Independence">declaration of independence</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">Somali Civil War</a> in 1991.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>At the Grand conference in <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a> held in 1991 many names for the country were suggested, including <i>Puntland</i>, in reference to Somaliland's location in the ancient <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Punt" title="Land of Punt">Land of Punt</a> and which is now the name of the <a href="/wiki/Puntland" title="Puntland">Puntland</a> state in neighbouring Somalia, and <i>Shankaroon</i>, meaning "better than five" in <a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a>, in reference to the five regions of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Somalia" title="Greater Somalia">Greater Somalia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Somaliland" title="History of Somaliland">History of Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Caves_in_Somaliland" title="Caves in Somaliland">Caves in Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See the <a href="/wiki/Laas_Geel" title="Laas Geel">Laas Geel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dhambalin" title="Dhambalin">Dhambalin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhaymoole" title="Dhaymoole">Dhaymoole</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg/220px-Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg/330px-Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg/440px-Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="634" data-file-height="357"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dhaymoole_Rock_art_in_Somaliland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Wild_animals" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild animals">Wild animals</a> depicted in the caves of <a href="/wiki/Dhaymoole" title="Dhaymoole">Dhaymoole</a>, many of which have gone extinct in the region.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somaliland has been inhabited since at least the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a>. During the Stone Age, the Doian and Hargeisan cultures flourished here.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The oldest evidence of burial customs in the Horn of Africa comes from cemeteries in Somaliland dating back to the 4th millennium BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The stone implements from the Jalelo site in the north were also characterized in 1909 as important artefacts demonstrating the archaeological universality during the Paleolithic between the East and the West.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to linguists, the first <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a>-speaking populations arrived in the region during the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period from the family's proposed <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_Urheimat" title="Afroasiatic Urheimat">urheimat</a> ("original homeland") in the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile Valley">Nile Valley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Laas_Geel" title="Laas Geel">Laas Geel</a> complex on the outskirts of <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a> in northwestern Somaliland dates back around 5,000 years, and has <a href="/wiki/Rock_art" title="Rock art">rock art</a> depicting both wild animals and decorated cows.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Cave_painting" title="Cave painting">cave paintings</a> are found in the northern <a href="/wiki/Dhambalin" title="Dhambalin">Dhambalin</a> region, which feature one of the earliest known depictions of a hunter on horseback. The rock art is in the distinctive Ethiopian-Arabian style, dated to 1,000 to 3,000 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Additionally, between the towns of <a href="/wiki/Las_Khorey" title="Las Khorey">Las Khorey</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Ayo" title="El Ayo">El Ayo</a> in eastern Somaliland lies <a href="/wiki/Karinhegane" title="Karinhegane">Karinhegane</a>, the site of numerous cave paintings of real and mythical animals. Each painting has an inscription below it, which collectively have been estimated to be around 2,500 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity_and_classical_era">Antiquity and classical era</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Somali_Architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali Architecture">Somali Architecture</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg/220px-Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg/330px-Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg/440px-Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sheekh_Isaaq.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The tomb of <a href="/wiki/Ishaaq_bin_Ahmed" title="Ishaaq bin Ahmed">Sheikh Isaaq</a>, the founding father of the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a> clan, in <a href="/wiki/Maydh" title="Maydh">Maydh</a>, Sanaag.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ancient <a href="/wiki/Pyramid" title="Pyramid">pyramidical</a> structures, <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum" title="Mausoleum">mausoleums</a>, ruined cities and stone walls, such as the <a href="/wiki/Wargaade_Wall" title="Wargaade Wall">Wargaade Wall</a>, are evidence of an old civilization that once thrived in the Somali peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-Nthos_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nthos-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> This civilization enjoyed a trading relationship with <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mycenaean_Greece" title="Mycenaean Greece">Mycenaean Greece</a> since the second millennium BCE, supporting the hypothesis that Somalia or adjacent regions were the location of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Punt" title="Land of Punt">Land of Punt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nthos_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nthos-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The Puntites traded <a href="/wiki/Myrrh" title="Myrrh">myrrh</a>, spices, gold, ebony, short-horned cattle, ivory and <a href="/wiki/Frankincense" title="Frankincense">frankincense</a> with the Egyptians, Phoenicians, <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">Babylonians</a>, Indians, Chinese and Romans through their commercial ports. An Egyptian expedition sent to Punt by the <a href="/wiki/Eighteenth_dynasty_of_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="Eighteenth dynasty of Egypt">18th dynasty</a> Queen <a href="/wiki/Hatshepsut" title="Hatshepsut">Hatshepsut</a> is recorded on the temple reliefs at <a href="/wiki/Deir_el-Bahari" title="Deir el-Bahari">Deir el-Bahari</a>, during the reign of the Puntite King Parahu and Queen Ati.<sup id="cite_ref-Nthos_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nthos-38">[38]</a></sup> In 2015, isotopic analysis of ancient baboon mummies from Punt that had been brought to Egypt as gifts indicated that the specimens likely originated from an area encompassing eastern Somalia and the Eritrea-Ethiopia corridor.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Camel" title="Camel">camel</a> is believed to have been domesticated in the Horn region sometime between the 2nd and 3rd millennium BCE. From there, it spread to Egypt and the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> During the classical period, the northern <a href="/wiki/Barbara_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbara (region)">Barbara</a> city-states of <a href="/wiki/Mosylon" title="Mosylon">Mosylon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opone" title="Opone">Opone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heis_(town)" title="Heis (town)">Mundus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulhar" title="Bulhar">Isis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malao" title="Malao">Malao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeila" title="Zeila">Avalites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essina" title="Essina">Essina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikon_(Somalia)" title="Nikon (Somalia)">Nikon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sarapion" title="Sarapion">Sarapion</a> developed a lucrative trade network, connecting with merchants from <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom" title="Ptolemaic Kingdom">Ptolemaic Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Persia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabaeans" title="Sabaeans">Saba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nabataean_Kingdom" title="Nabataean Kingdom">Nabataean Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. They used the ancient Somali maritime vessel known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Beden" title="Beden">beden</a></i> to transport their cargo.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Nabatea#Roman_annexation" class="mw-redirect" title="Nabatea">Roman conquest of the Nabataean Empire</a> and the Roman naval presence at <a href="/wiki/Aden" title="Aden">Aden</a> to curb piracy, Arab and Somali merchants agreed with the Romans to bar Indian ships from trading in the free port cities of the Arabian peninsula<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> to protect the interests of Somali and Arab merchants in the lucrative commerce between the Red and Mediterranean Seas.<sup id="cite_ref-EHW_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHW-45">[45]</a></sup> However, Indian merchants continued to trade in the port cities of the Somali peninsula, which was free from Roman interference.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For centuries, Indian merchants brought large quantities of cinnamon to Somalia and Arabia from <a href="/wiki/Ceylon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Spice Islands</a>. The source of the cinnamon and other spices is said to have been the best-kept secret of Arab and Somali merchants in their trade with the Roman and Greek world; the Romans and Greeks believed the source to have been the Somali peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The collusive agreement among Somali and Arab traders inflated the price of Indian and Chinese cinnamon in North Africa, the Near East, and Europe and made the cinnamon trade a very profitable revenue generator, especially for the Somali merchants through whose hands large quantities were shipped across sea and land routes.<sup id="cite_ref-EHW_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHW-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, more rock art sites with Sabaean and Himyarite writings in and around Hargeysa region were found, but some were bulldozed by developers.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_of_Islam_and_the_Middle_Ages">Birth of Islam and the Middle Ages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Somali_aristocratic_and_court_titles" title="Somali aristocratic and court titles">Somali aristocratic and court titles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ifat_Sultanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Ifat Sultanate">Ifat Sultanate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">Adal Sultanate</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG/220px-YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG/330px-YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG/440px-YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2379" data-file-height="1524"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:YagbeaSionBattlingAdaSultan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">Sultan of Adal</a> (right) and his troops battling King <a href="/wiki/Yagbe%27u_Seyon_of_Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Yagbe'u Seyon of Ethiopia">Yagbea-Sion</a> and his men. From <i>Le livre des Merveilles</i>, 15th century.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Various Somali Muslim kingdoms were established around this period in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewispohoa_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewispohoa-49">[49]</a></sup> In the 14th century, the <a href="/wiki/Zeila" title="Zeila">Zeila</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">Adal Sultanate</a> battled the forces of the Ethiopian emperor <a href="/wiki/Amda_Seyon_I" title="Amda Seyon I">Amda Seyon I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> later occupied <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a> and environs in the 1500s. <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">Muhammad Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pasha" title="Pasha">Pasha</a> of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, subsequently established a foothold in the area between 1821 and 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-Clifford_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clifford-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_sultanates">Early modern sultanates</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dervish_movement_(Somali)" title="Dervish movement (Somali)">Dervish movement (Somali)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaaq_Sultanate" title="Isaaq Sultanate">Isaaq Sultanate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern" class="mw-redirect" title="Early modern">early modern</a> period, successor states to the Adal Sultanate began to flourish in Somaliland. These included the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq_Sultanate" title="Isaaq Sultanate">Isaaq Sultanate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habr_Yunis_Sultanate" title="Habr Yunis Sultanate">Habr Yunis Sultanate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first engagement between Somalis of the region and the British was in 1825 and ended violently.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> This culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berbera_1827" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Berbera 1827">Battle of Berbera</a> and a subsequent trade agreement between the <a href="/wiki/Habr_Awal" title="Habr Awal">Habr Awal</a> and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> This was followed by a British treaty with the Governor of <a href="/wiki/Zeila" title="Zeila">Zeila</a> in 1840. An engagement was then started between the British and elders of <a href="/wiki/Garhajis" title="Garhajis">Habar Garhajis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habr_Je%27lo" title="Habr Je'lo">Habar Toljaala</a> clans of the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a> in 1855, followed a year later by the conclusion of the "Articles of Peace and Friendship" between the Habar Awal and <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>. These engagements between the British and Somali clans culminated in the formal treaties the British signed with the henceforth 'British Somaliland' clans, which took place between 1884 and 1886 (treaties were signed with the Habar Awal, Gadabursi, Habar Toljaala, Habar Garhajis, Esa, and the Warsangali clans), this paved the way for the British to establish a <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> in the region referred to as <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The British garrisoned the protectorate from <a href="/wiki/Aden_Settlement" class="mw-redirect" title="Aden Settlement">Aden</a> and administered it as part of <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="British Indian Empire">British India</a> until 1898. British Somaliland was then administered by the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Office">Foreign Office</a> until 1905, and afterwards by the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Office" title="Colonial Office">Colonial Office</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Somaliland">British Somaliland</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_campaign" title="Somaliland campaign">Somaliland campaign</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_campaign_(1920)" title="Somaliland campaign (1920)">Somaliland campaign (1920)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italian_conquest_of_British_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian conquest of British Somaliland">Italian conquest of British Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG/170px-Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG/255px-Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG/340px-Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Corriere_Della_Sera_-_17_agosto_1940_-_Offensiva_in_Africa_-_titolo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
          The Italian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Corriere_della_Sera" title="Corriere della Sera">Corriere della Sera</a></i> covering the start of the <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a> offensive
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Somaliland Campaign, also called the Anglo-Somali War or the Dervish War, was a series of military expeditions that took place between 1900 and 1920 in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>, pitting the <a href="/wiki/Dervish_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Dervish state">Dervishes</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Abdullah_Hassan" title="Mohammed Abdullah Hassan">Mohammed Abdullah Hassan</a> (nicknamed the "Mad Mullah") against the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The British were assisted in their offensives by the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire of Ethiopia">Ethiopians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italians</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> (1914–1918), Hassan also received aid from the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germans</a> and, for a time, from the Emperor <a href="/wiki/Iyasu_V_of_Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Iyasu V of Ethiopia">Iyasu V of Ethiopia</a>. The conflict ended when the British <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_campaign_(1920)" title="Somaliland campaign (1920)">aerially bombed</a> the Dervish capital of <a href="/wiki/Taleh" title="Taleh">Taleh</a> in February 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Fifth Expedition of the <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_campaign" title="Somaliland campaign">Somaliland campaign</a> in 1920 was the final <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> expedition against the <a href="/wiki/Dervish_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Dervish State">Dervish</a> forces of <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Abdullah_Hassan" title="Mohammed Abdullah Hassan">Mohammed Abdullah Hassan</a> (often called the "Mad Mullah" derogatorily by British), the <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">Somali</a> religious leader. Although most of the combat took place in January of the year, British troops had begun preparations for the assault as early as November 1919. The British forces included elements of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Camel_Corps" title="Somaliland Camel Corps">Somaliland Camel Corps</a>. After three weeks of battle, Hassan's Dervishes were defeated, bringing an effective end to their 20-year resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Italian conquest of British Somaliland was a military campaign in East Africa, which took place in August 1940 between forces of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a> and those of several British and <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">Commonwealth</a> countries. The Italian expedition was part of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="East African Campaign (World War II)">East African Campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_of_Somaliland">State of Somaliland</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/State_of_Somaliland" title="State of Somaliland">State of Somaliland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(State_of_Somaliland)" title="Independence Day (State of Somaliland)">Independence Day (State of Somaliland)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg/170px-Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg/255px-Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg/340px-Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg 2x" data-file-width="426" data-file-height="503"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_Flying_for_the_first_time_The_White_and_Blue_Somali_Flag_at_the_Independence_Celebrations_on_26_June_1960.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The White and Blue Somali Flag at the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(State_of_Somaliland)" title="Independence Day (State of Somaliland)">Independence</a> celebrations on 26 June 1960 when the prime minister of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Somaliland" title="State of Somaliland">State of Somaliland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Somaliland" title="President of Somaliland">second president of Somaliland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Haji_Ibrahim_Egal" title="Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal">Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal</a>, salute the flag.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In May 1960, the British government stated that it would be prepared to grant independence to the then <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> of British Somaliland, with the intention that the territory would unite with the <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a>-administered <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_Somaliland" title="Trust Territory of Somaliland">Trust Territory of Somaliland under Italian Administration</a> (the former <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The Legislative Council of British Somaliland passed a resolution in April 1960 requesting independence and union with the Trust Territory of Somaliland, which was scheduled to gain independence on 1 July that year. The legislative councils of both territories agreed to this proposal following a joint conference in <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wardheernews.com_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wardheernews.com-63">[63]</a></sup> On 26 June 1960, the former British Somaliland protectorate briefly obtained independence as the State of Somaliland, with the Trust Territory of Somaliland following suit five days later.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopædia_Britannica_2002_p.835_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopædia_Britannica_2002_p.835-12">[12]</a></sup> During its brief period of independence, the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Somaliland" title="State of Somaliland">State of Somaliland</a> garnered recognition from thirty-five sovereign states.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaplan257_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaplan257-64">[64]</a></sup> The following day, on 27 June 1960, the newly convened Somaliland Legislative Assembly approved a bill that would formally allow for the union of the State of Somaliland with the Trust Territory of Somaliland on 1 July 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-wardheernews.com_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wardheernews.com-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Somali_Republic">Somali Republic</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Somali_Republic" title="Somali Republic">Somali Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Somalia" title="Greater Somalia">Greater Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/1961_revolt_in_Somalia" title="1961 revolt in Somalia">1961 revolt in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 1 July 1960, the protectorate and the <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_Somaliland" title="Trust Territory of Somaliland">Trust Territory of Somaliland</a> (the former <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>) united as planned to form the <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somali Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-buluugleey.com_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buluugleey.com-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tmotss_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tmotss-66">[66]</a></sup> Inspired by <a href="/wiki/Somali_nationalism" title="Somali nationalism">Somali nationalism</a>, the northerners were initially enthusiastic about the union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichards201484–85_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichards201484–85-67">[67]</a></sup> A government was formed by <a href="/wiki/Abdullahi_Issa" title="Abdullahi Issa">Abdullahi Issa</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Aden_Abdullah_Osman_Daar" class="mw-redirect" title="Aden Abdullah Osman Daar">Aden Abdullah Osman Daar</a> as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Somalia">President</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abdirashid_Ali_Shermarke" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdirashid Ali Shermarke">Abdirashid Ali Shermarke</a> as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Somalia">Prime Minister</a> (later to become president, from 1967 to 1969). On 20 July 1961 and through a popular <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>, the Somali people ratified a new constitution, which was first drafted in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The constitution had little support in the former Somaliland, and was believed to favour the south. Many northerners boycotted the referendum in protest, and over 60% of those who voted in the north were against the new constitution. Regardless, the referendum passed, and Somaliland became quickly dominated by southerners. As result, dissatisfaction became widespread in the north, and support for the union plummeted. British-trained Somaliland officers attempted a <a href="/wiki/1961_revolt_in_Somalia" title="1961 revolt in Somalia">revolt to end the union in December 1961</a>. Their uprising failed, and Somaliland continued to be marginalized by the south during the next decades.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichards201484–85_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichards201484–85-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1967, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Haji_Ibrahim_Egal" title="Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal">Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal</a> became Prime Minister, a position to which he was appointed by Shermarke. Shermarke was assassinated two years later by one of his own bodyguards. His murder was quickly followed by a military <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> on 21 October 1969 (the day after his funeral), in which the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Somalia">Somalian Army</a> seized power without encountering armed opposition. The putsch was spearheaded by Major General <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Mohamed Siad Barre</a>, who at the time commanded the army.<sup id="cite_ref-Myswenvwp_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Myswenvwp-69">[69]</a></sup> The new regime would go on to rule Somalia for the next 22 years.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Somali_National_Movement.2C_Barre_persecution"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Somali_National_Movement,_Barre_persecution">Somali National Movement, Barre persecution</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Somali_National_Movement" title="Somali National Movement">Somali National Movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isaaq_genocide" title="Isaaq genocide">Isaaq genocide</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland,_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_(SNM),_1980s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Somaliland%2C_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_%28SNM%29%2C_1980s.jpg/250px-Somaliland%2C_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_%28SNM%29%2C_1980s.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Somaliland%2C_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_%28SNM%29%2C_1980s.jpg/375px-Somaliland%2C_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_%28SNM%29%2C_1980s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Somaliland%2C_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_%28SNM%29%2C_1980s.jpg/500px-Somaliland%2C_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_%28SNM%29%2C_1980s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="630"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland,_fighters_of_the_Somali_National_Movement_(SNM),_1980s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>SNM fighters, late 1980s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hargeisa_destroyed_by_Somali_government.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Hargeisa_destroyed_by_Somali_government.jpg/200px-Hargeisa_destroyed_by_Somali_government.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Hargeisa_destroyed_by_Somali_government.jpg/300px-Hargeisa_destroyed_by_Somali_government.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Hargeisa_destroyed_by_Somali_government.jpg/400px-Hargeisa_destroyed_by_Somali_government.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1744" data-file-height="1183"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:4z2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Up to 90% of <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a> (2nd largest city of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Republic" title="Somali Republic">Somali Republic</a>) was destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Somali_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali government">Somali government</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Moral_authority" title="Moral authority">moral authority</a> of Barre's government was gradually eroded, as many Somalis became disillusioned with life under military rule. By the mid-1980s, resistance movements supported by Ethiopia's communist <a href="/wiki/Derg" title="Derg">Derg</a> administration had sprung up across the country. Barre responded by ordering punitive measures against those he perceived as locally supporting the guerrillas, especially in the northern regions. The clampdown included bombing of cities, with the northwestern administrative centre of <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Somali_National_Movement" title="Somali National Movement">Somali National Movement</a> (SNM) stronghold, among the targeted areas in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-Locsg_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Locsg-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The bombardment was led by General <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Said_Hersi_Morgan" title="Mohammed Said Hersi Morgan">Mohammed Said Hersi Morgan</a>, Barre's son-in-law.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to Abou Jeng and other scholars, the Barre regime rule was marked by a targeted brutal persecution of the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a> clan.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Mohamed Haji Ingiriis and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Mullin_(politician)" title="Chris Mullin (politician)">Chris Mullin</a> state that the clampdown by the Barre regime against the Hargeisa-based Somali National Movement targeted the Isaaq clan, to which most members of the SNM belonged. They refer to the clampdown as the Isaaq genocide or Hargeisa holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>&nbsp;A <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> investigation concluded that the crime of genocide was "conceived, planned and perpetrated by the Somali Government against the Isaaq people".<sup id="cite_ref-Mburu_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mburu-77">[77]</a></sup> The number of civilian casualties is estimated to be between 50,000 and 100,000 according to various sources,<sup id="cite_ref-Peifer_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peifer-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jones_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-80">[80]</a></sup> while some reports estimate the total civilian deaths to be upwards of 200,000 Isaaq civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Along with the deaths, Barre regime bombarded and razed the second and third largest cities in Somalia, <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> This displaced an estimated 400,000 local residents to Hartasheikh in Ethiopia;<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> another 400,000 individuals were also internally displaced.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The counterinsurgency by the Barre regime against the SNM targeted the rebel group's civilian base of support, escalating into a genocidal onslaught against the Isaaq clan. This led to anarchy and violent campaigns by fragmented militias, which then wrested power at a local level.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The Barre regime's persecution was not limited to the Isaaq, as it targeted other clans such as the <a href="/wiki/Hawiye" title="Hawiye">Hawiye</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Richards2016p98_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richards2016p98-91">[91]</a></sup> The Barre regime collapsed in January 1991. Thereafter, as the political situation in Somaliland stabilized, the displaced people returned to their homes, the militias were demobilized or incorporated into the army, and tens of thousands of houses and businesses were reconstructed from rubble.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Somali_Civil_War">Somali Civil War</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">Somali Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Somaliland Declaration of Independence">Somaliland Declaration of Independence</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg/170px-Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg/255px-Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg/340px-Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hargeisa_War_Memorial_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hargeisa_War_Memorial" title="Hargeisa War Memorial">MiG monument in Hargeisa</a> commemorating Somaliland's breakaway from the rest of Somalia in 1991
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although the SNM at its inception had a unionist constitution, it eventually began to pursue independence, looking to secede from the rest of Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-Sqfirhbmsscf_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sqfirhbmsscf-93">[93]</a></sup> Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Abdirahman_Ahmed_Ali_Tuur" title="Abdirahman Ahmed Ali Tuur">Abdirahman Ahmed Ali Tuur</a>, the local administration declared the northwestern Somali territories independent at a conference held in <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a> between 27 April 1991 and 15 May 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Tuur then became the newly established Somaliland polity's first President, but subsequently renounced the separatist platform in 1994 and began instead to publicly seek and advocate reconciliation with the rest of Somalia under a power-sharing <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> system of governance.<sup id="cite_ref-Sqfirhbmsscf_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sqfirhbmsscf-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Haji_Ibrahim_Egal" title="Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal">Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal</a> was appointed as Tuur's successor in 1993 by the Grand Conference of National Reconciliation in <a href="/wiki/Borama" title="Borama">Borama</a>, which met for four months, leading to a gradual improvement in security, as well as a consolidation of the new territory.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Egal was reappointed in 1997, and remained in power until his death on 3 May 2002. The vice-president, <a href="/wiki/Dahir_Riyale_Kahin" title="Dahir Riyale Kahin">Dahir Riyale Kahin</a>, who was during the 1980s the highest-ranking <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Service_(Somalia)" title="National Security Service (Somalia)">National Security Service</a> (NSS) officer in <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a> in Siad Barre's government, was sworn in as president shortly afterward.<sup id="cite_ref-Albla_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Albla-96">[96]</a></sup> In 2003, Kahin became the first elected president of Somaliland.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/War_in_Somalia_(2006%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Somalia (2006–present)">war in southern Somalia</a> between <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabaab_(militant_group)" title="Al-Shabaab (militant group)">Islamist insurgents</a> on the one hand, and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Government_of_Somalia" title="Federal Government of Somalia">Federal Government of Somalia</a> and its <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> allies on the other, has for the most part not directly affected Somaliland, which, like neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Puntland" title="Puntland">Puntland</a>, has remained relatively stable.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2001_constitutional_referendum">2001 constitutional referendum</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2001_Somaliland_constitutional_referendum" title="2001 Somaliland constitutional referendum">2001 Somaliland constitutional referendum</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In August 2000, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Haji_Ibrahim_Egal" title="Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal">President Egal's government</a> distributed thousands of copies of the proposed constitution throughout Somaliland for consideration and review by the people. One critical clause of the 130 individual articles of the constitution would ratify Somaliland's self-declared independence and final separation from <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, restoring the nation's independence for the first time since 1960. In late March 2001, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Haji_Ibrahim_Egal" title="Muhammad Haji Ibrahim Egal">President Egal</a> set the date for the referendum on the Constitution for May 31, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A constitutional referendum was held in Somaliland on 31 May 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The referendum was held on a draft <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Somaliland" title="Constitution of Somaliland">constitution</a> that affirmed Somaliland's independence from <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>. 99.9% of eligible voters took part in the referendum and 97.1% of them voted in favour of the constitution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Somaliland" title="Politics of Somaliland">Politics of Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Somaliland" title="Elections in Somaliland">Elections in Somaliland</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Somaliland_politicians" title="List of Somaliland politicians">List of Somaliland politicians</a>
      </div>
