        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Muse_Bihi_Abdi" title="Muse Bihi Abdi">Muse Bihi Abdi</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/File:Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Somaliland.png" class="image"><img alt="Seal of the President of the Republic of Somaliland.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Somaliland.png/20px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Somaliland.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Somaliland.png/30px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Somaliland.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Somaliland.png/40px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Somaliland.png 2x" data-file-width="4480" data-file-height="4480"></a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Somaliland" title="President of Somaliland">President</a></small> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Abdirahman_Saylici" title="Abdirahman Saylici">Abdirahman Saylici</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_Somaliland.svg" class="image"><img alt="Emblem of Somaliland.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Emblem_of_Somaliland.svg/15px-Emblem_of_Somaliland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Emblem_of_Somaliland.svg/23px-Emblem_of_Somaliland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Emblem_of_Somaliland.svg/30px-Emblem_of_Somaliland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Somaliland" title="Vice President of Somaliland">Vice President</a></small> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <i>guurti</i> worked with rebel leaders to set up a new government, and was incorporated into the governance structure, becoming the Parliament's <a href="/wiki/House_of_Elders_of_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Elders of Somaliland">House of Elders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gettleman_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gettleman-102">[102]</a></sup> The government became in essence a "power-sharing coalition of Somaliland's main clans," with seats in the Upper and Lower houses proportionally allocated to clans according to a predetermined formula, although not all clans are satisfied with their representation. In 2002, after several extensions of this interim government, Somaliland transitioned to multi-party democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The election was limited to three parties, in an attempt to create ideology based elections rather than clan-based elections.<sup id="cite_ref-Gettleman_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gettleman-102">[102]</a></sup> As of December 2014, Somaliland has three <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Somaliland" title="List of political parties in Somaliland">political parties</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Peace,_Unity,_and_Development_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace, Unity, and Development Party">Peace, Unity, and Development Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/For_Justice_and_Development" title="For Justice and Development">Justice and Development Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wadani_(political_party)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wadani (political party)">Wadani</a>. Under the Somaliland Constitution, a maximum of three political parties is allowed.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Executive is led by an elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_Somaliland" title="President of Somaliland">president</a>, whose government includes a vice-president and a Council of Ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-Administration_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Administration-105">[105]</a></sup> The Council of Ministers, who are responsible for the normal running of government, are nominated by the President and approved by the Parliament's House of Representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Cabinet_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cabinet-106">[106]</a></sup> The President must approve bills passed by the Parliament before they come into effect.<sup id="cite_ref-Administration_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Administration-105">[105]</a></sup> Presidential elections are confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Electoral_Commission_(Somaliland)" title="National Electoral Commission (Somaliland)">National Electoral Commission of Somaliland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-afp_2010-07-01_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp_2010-07-01-107">[107]</a></sup> The President can serve a maximum of two five-year terms. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somalia_(Somaliland),_Hargeisa,_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%2C_Hargeisa%2C_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG/170px-Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%2C_Hargeisa%2C_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%2C_Hargeisa%2C_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG/255px-Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%2C_Hargeisa%2C_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%2C_Hargeisa%2C_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG/340px-Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%2C_Hargeisa%2C_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3219" data-file-height="2375"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somalia_(Somaliland),_Hargeisa,_House_of_Representatives_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of Somaliland">House of Representatives</a> (Lower House) of the Somaliland Parliament.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Legislative power is held by the <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Somaliland" title="Parliament of Somaliland">Parliament</a>. Its upper house is the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Elders_of_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Elders of Somaliland">House of Elders</a>, this chamber is chaired by <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_Mohamoud_Adan" title="Suleiman Mohamoud Adan">Suleiman Mohamoud Adan</a>, and the lower house is the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of Somaliland">House of Representatives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Administration_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Administration-105">[105]</a></sup> The lower house is chaired by <a href="/wiki/Bashe_Mohamed_Farah" title="Bashe Mohamed Farah">Bashe Mohamed Farah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Each house has 82 members. Members of the House of Elders are elected indirectly by local communities for six-year terms. The House of Elders shares power in passing laws with the House of Representatives, and also has the role of solving internal conflicts, and exclusive power to extend the terms of the President and representatives under circumstances that make an election impossible. Members of the House of Representatives are directly elected by the people for five-year terms. The House of Representatives shares voting power with the House of Elders, though it can pass a law that the House of Elders rejects if it votes for the law by a two-thirds majority, and has absolute power in financial matters and confirmation of Presidential appointments (except for the <a href="/wiki/Adan_Haji_Ali" title="Adan Haji Ali">Chief Justice of the Supreme Court</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The judicial system is divided into district courts, (which deal with matters of family law and succession, lawsuits for amounts up to 3 million <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_shilling" title="Somaliland shilling">SLSH</a>, criminal cases punishable by up to 3 years imprisonment or 3 million SL fines, and crimes committed by juveniles), regional courts (which deal with lawsuits and criminal cases not within the jurisdiction of district courts, labour and employment claims, and local government elections), regional appeals courts (which deal with all appeals from the district and regional courts), and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court" title="Supreme court">Supreme Court</a> (which deals with issues between courts and in government, and reviews its own decisions), which is the highest court and also functions as the Constitutional Court.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Citizenship"></span>Somaliland nationality law defines who is a Somaliland citizen,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> as well as the procedures by which one may be <a href="/wiki/Naturalised" class="mw-redirect" title="Naturalised">naturalised</a> into Somaliland citizenship or <a href="/wiki/Renunciation_of_citizenship" title="Renunciation of citizenship">renounce it</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg/170px-Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg/255px-Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg/340px-Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="680"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_UCID_elections_rally.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Women in the Somaliland, wearing the colors of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Somaliland" title="Flag of Somaliland">Somaliland flag</a>, prior to parliamentary elections in 2005.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Somaliland government continues to apply the 1962 penal code of the Somali Republic. As such, homosexual acts are illegal in the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-ILGA_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ILGA-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Freedom House ranks the Somaliland government as partly democratic.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Seth Kaplan (2011) argues that in contrast to southern Somalia and adjacent territories, Somaliland, the secessionist northwestern portion of Somalia, has built a more democratic mode of governance from the bottom up, with virtually no foreign assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaplan248252_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaplan248252-115">[115]</a></sup> Specifically, Kaplan suggests that Somaliland has the most democratic political system in the Horn of Africa because it has been largely insulated from the extremist elements in the rest of Somalia and has viable electoral and legislative systems as well as a robust private sector-dominated economy, unlike neighbouring authoritarian governments. He largely attributes this to Somaliland's integration of customary laws and tradition with modern state structures, which he indicates most post-colonial states in Africa and the Middle East have not had the opportunity to do. Kaplan asserts that this has facilitated cohesiveness and conferred greater governmental legitimacy in Somaliland, as has the territory's comparatively homogeneous population, relatively equitable income distribution, a common fear of the south, and absence of interference by outside forces, which has obliged local politicians to observe a degree of accountability.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaplan248249253_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaplan248249253-116">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Somaliland" title="Foreign relations of Somaliland">Foreign relations of Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_President_of_Somaliland,_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister,_Mamadi_Toure.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_President_of_Somaliland%2C_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister%2C_Mamadi_Toure.jpg/220px-The_President_of_Somaliland%2C_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister%2C_Mamadi_Toure.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_President_of_Somaliland%2C_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister%2C_Mamadi_Toure.jpg/330px-The_President_of_Somaliland%2C_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister%2C_Mamadi_Toure.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_President_of_Somaliland%2C_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister%2C_Mamadi_Toure.jpg/440px-The_President_of_Somaliland%2C_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister%2C_Mamadi_Toure.jpg 2x" data-file-width="563" data-file-height="375"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_President_of_Somaliland,_Musa_Bihi_Abdi_And_the_Guinean_Foreign_minister,_Mamadi_Toure.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The President of Somaliland <a href="/wiki/Muse_Bihi_Abdi" title="Muse Bihi Abdi">Muse Bihi Abdi</a> during a visit to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Guinea">Republic of Guinea</a>. He received a high-ranking delegation headed by the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Guinea)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (Guinea)"> Minister of Foreign Affairs of Guinea</a> Mamadi Touré in 2019.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somaliland has political contacts with its neighbours <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a><sup id="cite_ref-Future_recognition_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Future_recognition-117">[117]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Djibouti_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Djibouti-118">[118]</a></sup> non-UN member state <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China (Taiwan)</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Diplo_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diplo-120">[120]</a></sup> as well as with <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Future_recognition_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Future_recognition-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and the micro-nation of <a href="/wiki/Liberland" title="Liberland">Liberland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> On 17 January 2007, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) sent a delegation for foreign affairs to discuss future co-operation.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU) has also sent a foreign minister to discuss the future of international acknowledgment, and on 29 and 30 January 2007, the ministers stated that they would discuss acknowledgement with the organisation's member states.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In early 2006, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Wales">National Assembly of Wales</a> extended an official invitation to the Somaliland government to attend the royal opening of the <a href="/wiki/Senedd_building" title="Senedd building">Senedd</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>. The move was seen as an act of recognition by the Welsh Assembly of the breakaway government's legitimacy. The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a> made no comment on the invitation. Wales is home to a significant Somali <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> community from Somaliland.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, a delegation led by President Kahin was present at the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Heads_of_Government_Meeting_2007" title="Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting 2007">Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kampala" title="Kampala">Kampala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>. Although Somaliland has applied to join the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> under <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">observer status</a>, its application is still pending.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 24 September 2010, <a href="/wiki/Johnnie_Carson" title="Johnnie Carson">Johnnie Carson</a>, Assistant Secretary of State for African Affairs, stated that the United States would be modifying its strategy in Somalia and would seek deeper engagement with the governments of Somaliland and Puntland while continuing to support the Somali Transitional Government.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Carson said the US would send aid workers and diplomats to Puntland and Somaliland and alluded to the possibility of future development projects. However, Carson emphasised that the US would not extend formal recognition to either region.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg/220px-Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg/330px-Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg/440px-Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_Foreign_Minister_Hagi_Mohamoud_with_Taiwan_President_Tsai_Ing-wen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Somaliland Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Yasin_Haji_Mohamoud" title="Yasin Haji Mohamoud">Hagi Mohamoud</a> with Taiwan President <a href="/wiki/Tsai_Ing-wen" title="Tsai Ing-wen">Tsai Ing-wen</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The then-UK Minister for Africa, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bellingham_(Norfolk_MP)" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Bellingham (Norfolk MP)">Henry Bellingham</a> MP, met President Silanyo of Somaliland in November 2010 to discuss ways in which to increase the UK's engagement with Somaliland.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> President Silanyo said during his visit to London: "We have been working with the international community and the international community has been engaging with us, giving us assistance and working with us in our democratisation and development programmes. And we are very happy with the way the international community has been dealing with us, particularly the UK, the US, other European nations, and our neighbours who continue to seek recognition."<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Recognition of Somaliland by the UK has also been supported by the <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a>, which came 3rd in the popular vote at the 2015 General Election. The leader of UKIP, <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Farage" title="Nigel Farage">Nigel Farage</a>, met with Ali Aden Awale, Head of the Somaliland UK Mission on Somaliland's national day, 18 May, in 2015, to express UKIP's support for Somaliland. Nigel Farage said that "Somaliland has been a beacon of peace, democracy and the Rule of Law, in the Horn of Africa for the past 24 years. It is about time the UK and the rest of the international community recognised Somaliland's case for recognition. It's about time peace was rewarded. For the UK to turn its back on its legitimate demands for sovereignty, is wrong. It is extraordinary that we have not been lobbying for their admittance to the Commonwealth. In recent years, we have supported the admission of countries such as Mozambique, which have no historic links to Britain, but Somaliland, a former protectorate, is left in the cold. This must change".<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, Somaliland and the neighbouring Puntland region each entered a security-related <a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding" title="Memorandum of understanding">memorandum of understanding</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>. Following the framework of an earlier agreement signed between the Transitional Federal Government and Seychelles, the memorandum is "for the transfer of convicted persons to prisons in 'Puntland' and 'Somaliland'."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 July 2020, Somaliland and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> signed an agreement to set up representative offices to promote cooperation between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Cooperation between the two polities on education, maritime security, and medicine began in 2009, and Taiwanese staff entered Somaliland in February 2020 to prepare for the representative office.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_disputes">Border disputes</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

      </div>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somaliland continues to claim the entire area of the former <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-const_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-const-16">[16]</a></sup> It is currently in control of the vast majority of the former British Somaliland, with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Las_Qoray_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Qoray District">Las Qoray District</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a> region, which is under the control of neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Puntland" title="Puntland">Puntland</a>. </p>
      <p>Tensions between Puntland and Somaliland escalated into violence several times between 2002 and 2009. In October 2004, and again in April and October 2007, armed forces of Somaliland and Puntland clashed near the town of <a href="/wiki/Las_Anod" title="Las Anod">Las Anod</a>, the capital of Sool region. In October 2007, Somaliland troops took control of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> While celebrating Puntland's 11th anniversary on 2 August 2009, Puntland officials vowed to recapture Las Anod. While Somaliland claims independent statehood and therefore "split up" the "old" Somalia, Puntland works for the re-establishment of a united but <a href="/wiki/Federal_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal state">federal</a> Somali state.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somaliland forces took control of the town of <a href="/wiki/Las_Qorey" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Qorey">Las Qorey</a> in eastern <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a> on 10 July 2008, along with positions 5&nbsp;km (3&nbsp;mi) east of the town. The defence forces completed their operations on 9 July 2008 after the Maakhir and Puntland militia in the area left their positions,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> but control of the territory was later assumed by Puntland as Maakhir was incorporated into the autonomous region in January 2009.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In the late 2000s, HBM-SSC (Hoggaanka Badbaadada iyo Mideynta SSC), a local unionist group based in <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a> was formed with the goal to establish its own regional administration (Sool, Sanaag and Cayn, or SSC).<sup id="cite_ref-Sqfirhbmsscf_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sqfirhbmsscf-93">[93]</a></sup> This later evolved into <a href="/wiki/Khatumo_State" title="Khatumo State">Khatumo State</a>, which was established in 2012. The local administration and its constituents does not recognise the Somaliland government's claim to sovereignty or to its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Srwiks_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Srwiks-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 20 October 2017 in <a href="/wiki/Aynabo" class="mw-redirect" title="Aynabo">Aynabo</a>, an agreement was signed with the Somaliland government which stipulated the amendment of Somaliland's constitution and to integrate the organisation into the Somaliland government.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> This signalled the end of the organisation even though it was an unpopular event amongst the <a href="/wiki/Dhulbahante" title="Dhulbahante">Dhulbahante</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-144">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Armed_Forces" title="Somaliland Armed Forces">Somaliland Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg/220px-Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg/330px-Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg/440px-Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Commemoration_of_the_27th_Anniversary_of_the_Establishment_of_the_Somaliland_National_Army.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Commemoration (on 2 February 2021) of the 27th anniversary of the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_National_Army" title="Somaliland National Army">Somaliland National Army</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Armed_Forces" title="Somaliland Armed Forces">Somaliland Armed Forces</a> are the main military command in Somaliland. Along with the <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Police" title="Somaliland Police">Somaliland Police</a> and all other internal security forces, they are overseen by Somaliland's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Somaliland)" title="Ministry of Defence (Somaliland)">Ministry of Defence</a>. The current head of Somaliland's Armed Forces is the Minister of Defence, <a href="/wiki/Abdiqani_Mohamoud_Aateye" title="Abdiqani Mohamoud Aateye">Abdiqani Mohamoud Aateye</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Following the declaration of independence, various pre-existing militia affiliated with different clans were absorbed into a centralised military structure. The resultant large military takes up around half of the country's budget, but the action served to help prevent inter-clan violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Mesfin_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mesfin-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2–3</span></sup> </p>
      <p>The Somaliland Army consists of twelve divisions equipped primarily with light weaponry, though it is equipped with some <a href="/wiki/Howitzer" title="Howitzer">howitzers</a> and mobile <a href="/wiki/Rocket_launcher" title="Rocket launcher">rocket launchers</a>. Its armoured vehicles and tanks are mostly of Soviet design, though there are some ageing Western vehicles and tanks in its arsenal. The Somaliland Navy (often referred to as a Coast Guard by the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>), despite a crippling lack of equipment and formal training, has apparently had some success at curbing both piracy and illegal fishing within Somaliland waters.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Somaliland" title="Regions of Somaliland">Regions of Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_regions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Somaliland_regions.svg/310px-Somaliland_regions.svg.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Somaliland_regions.svg/465px-Somaliland_regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Somaliland_regions.svg/620px-Somaliland_regions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1006" data-file-height="764"></a>

           <li>
            <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">

            </div></li>
           <li>
            <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">

            </div></li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Currently Somaliland is divided into six regions: Awdal, Sahil, Maroodi-Jeeh, Togdheer, Sanaag and Sool. </p>
      <p>The regions are divided into eighteen administrative districts. </p>
      <p>The following regions are taken from <i>Michael Walls: State Formation in Somaliland: Bringing Deliberation to Institutionalism</i> from 2011, <i>Somaliland: The Strains of Success</i> from 2015 and ActionAID, a humanitarian organization currently active in Somaliland.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="Geography of Somaliland">Geography of Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_habitat">Location and habitat</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_sat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Somaliland_sat.jpg/220px-Somaliland_sat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Somaliland_sat.jpg/330px-Somaliland_sat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Somaliland_sat.jpg/440px-Somaliland_sat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1344" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_sat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Satellite image of Somaliland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somaliland is situated in the northwest of recognised Somalia. It lies between 08°N and 11°30'N, and between 42°30'E and 49°00'E.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Puntland" title="Puntland">Puntland</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> to the east. Somaliland has a 850 kilometres (528&nbsp;mi) coastline with the majority lying along the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mesfin_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mesfin-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>1</span></sup> In terms of landmass, Somaliland has an area of 176,120&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (68,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-auto_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somaliland's climate is a mixture of wet and dry conditions. The northern part of the region is hilly, and in many places the altitude ranges between 900 and 2,100 metres (3,000 and 6,900&nbsp;ft) above sea level. The <a href="/wiki/Awdal" title="Awdal">Awdal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahil,_Somaliland" title="Sahil, Somaliland">Sahil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maroodi_Jeex" title="Maroodi Jeex">Maroodi Jeex</a> (Woqooyi Galbeed) regions are fertile and mountainous, while <a href="/wiki/Togdheer" title="Togdheer">Togdheer</a> is mostly <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-arid">semi-desert</a> with little fertile greenery around. The Awdal region is also known for its offshore islands, <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a>. </p>
      <p>A scrub-covered, semi-desert plain referred as the <i><a href="/wiki/Guban" title="Guban">Guban</a></i> lies parallel to the Gulf of Aden littoral. With a width of twelve kilometres (7.5 miles) in the west to as little as two kilometres (1.2 miles) in the east, the plain is bisected by watercourses that are essentially beds of dry sand except during the rainy seasons. When the rains arrive, the Guban's low bushes and grass clumps transform into lush vegetation.<sup id="cite_ref-Hadden_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hadden-154">[154]</a></sup> This coastal strip is part of the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_xeric_grasslands_and_shrublands" title="Ethiopian xeric grasslands and shrublands">Ethiopian xeric grasslands and shrublands</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cal_Madow" title="Cal Madow">Cal Madow</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain range</a> in the eastern part of the country. Extending from the northwest of <a href="/wiki/Erigavo" title="Erigavo">Erigavo</a> to several kilometres west of the city of <a href="/wiki/Bosaso" title="Bosaso">Bosaso</a> in neighbouring Somalia, it features Somaliland's highest <a href="/wiki/Summit_(topography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Summit (topography)">peak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shimbiris" class="mw-redirect" title="Shimbiris">Shimbiris</a>, which sits at an elevation of about 2,416 metres (7,927&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-2009factbook_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009factbook-4">[4]</a></sup> The rugged east–west ranges of the Karkaar Mountains also lie to the interior of the Gulf of Aden littoral.<sup id="cite_ref-Hadden_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hadden-154">[154]</a></sup> In the central regions, the northern mountain ranges give way to shallow plateaus and typically dry watercourses that are referred to locally as the <i><a href="/wiki/Ogo_Mountains" title="Ogo Mountains">Ogo</a></i>. The Ogo's western plateau, in turn, gradually merges into the <a href="/wiki/Haud" title="Haud">Haud</a>, an important grazing area for livestock.<sup id="cite_ref-Hadden_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hadden-154">[154]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed"> 
       <li class="gallerycaption">Landscapes of Somaliland</li> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">
        <div style="width: 162px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Lamadayawaterfalls6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Lamadayawaterfalls6.jpg/240px-Lamadayawaterfalls6.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Lamadayawaterfalls6.jpg/360px-Lamadayawaterfalls6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Lamadayawaterfalls6.jpg/480px-Lamadayawaterfalls6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375"></a>
          </div>
         </div> 
         <div class="gallerytext"> 
          <p><a href="/wiki/Lamadaya" title="Lamadaya">Lamadaya</a> are waterfalls located in the <a href="/wiki/Cal_Madow" title="Cal Madow">Cal Madow</a> mountain. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div></li> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">
        <div style="width: 162px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Somalia_(Somaliland)(168).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%28168%29.jpg/240px-Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%28168%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%28168%29.jpg/360px-Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%28168%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%28168%29.jpg/480px-Somalia_%28Somaliland%29%28168%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a>

         </div> 
        </div></li> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">
        <div style="width: 162px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Almadow_Overview.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Almadow_Overview.JPG/240px-Almadow_Overview.JPG" decoding="async" width="160" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Almadow_Overview.JPG/360px-Almadow_Overview.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Almadow_Overview.JPG/480px-Almadow_Overview.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a>
          </div>
         </div> 
         <div class="gallerytext"> 
          <p>View of the <a href="/wiki/Cal_Madow" title="Cal Madow">Cal Madow</a> Mountains, home to numerous endemic species. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div></li> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215.33333333333px">
        <div style="width: 215.33333333333px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 213.33333333333px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
