      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg/290px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg/435px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg/580px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="719" data-file-height="350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Somaliland_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Köppen climate classification of Somaliland.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somaliland&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2021</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Somaliland is located north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>. It is semi-arid. The average daily temperatures range from 25 to 35&nbsp;°C (77 to 95&nbsp;°F). The sun passes vertically overhead twice a year, on 22 March and 23 September. Somaliland consists of three main topographic zones: a coastal plain (Guban), the coastal range (Oogo), and a plateau (Hawd). The coastal plain is a zone with high temperatures and low rainfall. Summer temperatures in the region easily average over 100&nbsp;°F (38&nbsp;°C). However, temperatures come down during the winter, and both human and livestock populations increase dramatically in the region. </p>
      <p>The coastal range (Ogo) is a high plateau to the immediate south of Guban. Its elevation ranges from 6,000 feet (1,800&nbsp;m) above sea level in the West to 7,000 feet (2,100&nbsp;m) in the East. Rainfall is heavier there than in Guban, although it varies considerably within the zone. The plateau (Hawd) region lies to the south of Ogo range. It is generally more heavily populated during the wet season, when surface water is available. It is also an important area for grazing. Somalilanders recognize four seasons in the year; GU and Hagaa comprise spring and summer in that order, and Dayr and Jiilaal correspond to autumn and winter respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (May 2021)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The average annual rainfall is 446 millimetres (17.6&nbsp;in) in some parts of country according to availability of rain gauge, and most of it comes during Gu and Dayr. GU, which is the first, or major, rainy season (late March, April, May, and early June), experiences the heaviest rainfall in Ogo range and Hawd. This constitutes the period of fresh grazing and abundant surface water. It is also the breeding season for livestock. Hagaa (from late June through August) is usually dry although there are often some scattered showers in the Ogo range, these are known as Karan rains. Hagaa tends to be hot and windy in most parts of the country. Deyr (September, October, and early November), which roughly corresponds to autumn, is the second, or minor, wet season; the amount of precipitation is generally less than that of Gu. Jilaal, or winter, falls in the coolest and driest months of the year (from late November to early March). It is a season of thirst. Hawd receive virtually no rainfall in winter. The rainfall in the Guban zone, known as "Hays", comes from December to February. The humidity of the country varies from 63% in the dry season to 82% in the wet season.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Somaliland" title="Economy of Somaliland">Economy of Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_Shillings.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Somaliland_Shillings.jpg/170px-Somaliland_Shillings.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Somaliland_Shillings.jpg/255px-Somaliland_Shillings.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Somaliland_Shillings.jpg/340px-Somaliland_Shillings.jpg 2x" data-file-width="513" data-file-height="615"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_Shillings.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>500 Somaliland Shillings, 1000 Somaliland Shillings, 5000 Somaliland Shillings.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_shilling" title="Somaliland shilling">Somaliland shilling</a>, which cannot easily be exchanged outside Somaliland on account of the nation's lack of recognition, is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Somaliland" title="Bank of Somaliland">Bank of Somaliland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>, which was established constitutionally in 1994. </p>
      <p>Since Somaliland is unrecognised, international donors have found it difficult to provide aid. As a result, the government relies mainly upon tax receipts and <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> from the large <a href="/wiki/Somali_diaspora" title="Somali diaspora">Somali diaspora</a>, which contribute immensely to Somaliland's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-157">[157]</a></sup> Remittances come to Somaliland through <a href="/wiki/Informal_value_transfer_system" title="Informal value transfer system">money transfer companies</a>, the largest of which is <a href="/wiki/Dahabshiil" title="Dahabshiil">Dahabshiil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> one of the few Somali money transfer companies that conform to modern money-transfer regulations. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimates that remittances worth approximately US$1 billion reach Somalia annually from <a href="/wiki/%C3%89migr%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Émigrés">émigrés</a> working in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf states</a>, Europe and the United States. Analysts say that Dahabshiil may handle around two-thirds of that figure and as much as half of it reaches Somaliland alone.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the late 1990s, service provisions have significantly improved through limited government provisions and contributions from <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organisations" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-governmental organisations">non-governmental organisations</a>, religious groups, the international community (especially the diaspora), and the growing private sector. Local and municipal governments have been developing key public service provisions such as water in Hargeisa and education, electricity, and security in Berbera.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-157">[157]</a></sup> In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Banque_pour_le_Commerce_et_l%27Industrie_%E2%80%93_Mer_Rouge" title="Banque pour le Commerce et l'Industrie – Mer Rouge">Banque pour le Commerce et l'Industrie – Mer Rouge</a> (BCIMR), based in <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>, opened a branch in <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a> and became the first bank in the country since the 1990 collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Somalia" title="Central Bank of Somalia">Commercial and Savings Bank of Somalia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Dahabshil_Bank_International" title="Dahabshil Bank International">Dahabshil Bank International</a> became the region's first commercial bank.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> In 2017 <a href="/wiki/Premier_Bank" title="Premier Bank">Premier Bank</a> from Mogadishu opened a branch in Hargeisa.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">Telecommunications</a> companies serving Somaliland include <a href="/wiki/Telesom" title="Telesom">Telesom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Telesom also offers among the cheapest international calling rates at US$0.2 less than its nearest competitor.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Somtel" title="Somtel">Somtel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telcom_(Somalia)" title="Telcom (Somalia)">Telcom</a> and <a href="/wiki/NationLink_Telecom" title="NationLink Telecom">NationLink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Livestock is the backbone of Somaliland's economy. Sheep, camels, and cattle are shipped from the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Berbera" title="Port of Berbera">Berbera port</a> and sent to Gulf Arab countries, such as Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The country is home to some of the largest livestock markets, known in Somali as <i>seylad</i>, in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>, with as many as 10,000 heads of sheep and goats sold daily in the markets of <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yirowe" title="Yirowe">Yirowe</a>, many of whom shipped to <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Gulf states</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Berbera" title="Port of Berbera">port</a> of <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> The markets handle livestock from all over the Horn of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> is generally considered to be a potentially successful industry, especially in the production of <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">cereals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horticulture" title="Horticulture">horticulture</a>. Mining also has potential, though simple <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">quarrying</a> represents the extent of current operations, despite the presence of diverse quantities of mineral deposits.<sup id="cite_ref-profile_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Somaliland" title="Tourism in Somaliland">Tourism in Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain,_Hargeisa,_Somalilanad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain%2C_Hargeisa%2C_Somalilanad.jpg/220px-Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain%2C_Hargeisa%2C_Somalilanad.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain%2C_Hargeisa%2C_Somalilanad.jpg/330px-Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain%2C_Hargeisa%2C_Somalilanad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain%2C_Hargeisa%2C_Somalilanad.jpg/440px-Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain%2C_Hargeisa%2C_Somalilanad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Naasa_Hablood_-_Virgin%27s_Breast_Mountain,_Hargeisa,_Somalilanad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Naasa_Hablood" title="Naasa Hablood">Naasa Hablood</a>, also known as Virgin's Breast Mountain.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Rock_art" title="Rock art">rock art</a> and caves at <a href="/wiki/Laas_Geel" title="Laas Geel">Laas Geel</a>, situated on the outskirts of <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>, are a popular local tourist attraction. Totaling ten caves, they were discovered by a <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> archaeological team in 2002 and are believed to date back around 5,000 years. The government and locals keep the <a href="/wiki/Cave_painting" title="Cave painting">cave paintings</a> safe and only a restricted number of tourists are allowed entry.<sup id="cite_ref-Ggsesl_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ggsesl-170">[170]</a></sup> Other notable sights include the Freedom Arch in Hargeisa and the <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa_War_Memorial" title="Hargeisa War Memorial">War Memorial</a> in the city centre. Natural attractions are very common around the region. The <a href="/wiki/Naasa_Hablood" title="Naasa Hablood">Naasa Hablood</a> are twin hills located on the outskirts of Hargeisa that Somalis in the region consider to be a majestic natural landmark.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (May 2021)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Ministry of Tourism has also encouraged travellers to visit historic towns and cities in Somaliland. The historic town of <a href="/wiki/Sheekh" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheekh">Sheekh</a> is located near Berbera and is home to old British colonial buildings that have remained untouched for over forty years. <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a> also houses historic and impressive <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman architectural</a> buildings. Another equally famous historic city is <a href="/wiki/Zeila" title="Zeila">Zeila</a>. Zeila was once part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, a dependency of <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and a major trade city during the 19th century. The city has been visited for its old colonial landmarks, offshore <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a> and coral reefs, towering cliffs, and beach. The <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> culture of Somaliland has also attracted tourists. Most nomads live in the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-171">[171]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png/170px-Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png/255px-Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png/340px-Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png 2x" data-file-width="355" data-file-height="360"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Berbera_Airport_Jun_2020.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Berbera_Airport" title="Berbera Airport">Berbera Airport</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bus services operate in <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabiley" title="Gabiley">Gabiley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borama" title="Borama">Borama</a>. There are also road transportation services between the major towns and adjacent villages, which are operated by different types of vehicles. Among these are <a href="/wiki/Taxi" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxi">taxis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minibus" title="Minibus">minibuses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Light_goods_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Light goods vehicle">light goods vehicles</a> (LGV).<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most prominent airlines serving Somaliland is <a href="/wiki/Daallo_Airlines" title="Daallo Airlines">Daallo Airlines</a>, a Somali-owned private carrier with regular international flights that emerged after <a href="/wiki/Somali_Airlines" title="Somali Airlines">Somali Airlines</a> ceased operations. <a href="/wiki/African_Express_Airways" title="African Express Airways">African Express Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines" title="Ethiopian Airlines">Ethiopian Airlines</a> also fly from airports in Somaliland to <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_(city)" title="Djibouti (city)">Djibouti City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, and offer flights for the <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a> pilgrimages via the <a href="/wiki/Egal_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Egal International Airport">Egal International Airport</a> in Hargeisa. Other major airports in the region include the <a href="/wiki/Berbera_Airport" title="Berbera Airport">Berbera Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span></h3> 
      <p>In June 2016, the Somaliland government signed an agreement with <a href="/wiki/DP_World" title="DP World">DP World</a> to manage the strategic port of <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a> with the aim of enhancing productive capacity and acting as an alternative port for landlocked Ethiopia.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_exploration">Oil exploration</span></h3> 
      <p>In August 2012, the Somaliland government awarded <a href="/wiki/Genel_Energy" title="Genel Energy">Genel Energy</a> a license to explore oil within its territory. Results of a surface seep study completed early in 2015 confirmed the outstanding potential offered in the SL-10B, SL-13, and Oodweyne blocks, with estimated oil reserves of 1 billion barrel each.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Genel Energy is set to drill an exploration well for SL-10B and SL-13 block in Buur-Dhaab, 20 kilometers northwest of <a href="/wiki/Aynabo" class="mw-redirect" title="Aynabo">Aynabo</a> by the end of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_clan_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Somaliland_clan_map.png/280px-Somaliland_clan_map.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Somaliland_clan_map.png/420px-Somaliland_clan_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Somaliland_clan_map.png/560px-Somaliland_clan_map.png 2x" data-file-width="6968" data-file-height="3829"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somaliland_clan_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Somaliland clan map
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg/280px-Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg/420px-Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg/560px-Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg 2x" data-file-width="757" data-file-height="360"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Distribution_of_Somaliland_population_by_age_and_sex_according_to_residence_report_2020.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population per age group
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somaliland's population was estimated at approximately 3.5 million in 2014. 52.9% of this population was estimated to be urban, 33.8% nomadic, 11% rural, and 2.4% were <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" class="mw-redirect" title="Internally displaced persons">internally displaced persons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Gadabuursi" title="Gadabuursi">Gadabuursi</a> subclan of the <a href="/wiki/Dir_(clan)" title="Dir (clan)">Dir</a> are the predominant clan of the <a href="/wiki/Awdal" title="Awdal">Awdal</a> region,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> where there is also a sizeable minority of the <a href="/wiki/Issa_(clan)" title="Issa (clan)">Issa</a> subclan of the <a href="/wiki/Dir_(clan)" title="Dir (clan)">Dir</a> who mainly inhabit the <a href="/wiki/Zeila_District" title="Zeila District">Zeila district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Janzen_von_Vitzthum_Somali_Studies_International_Association_2001_p._132_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janzen_von_Vitzthum_Somali_Studies_International_Association_2001_p._132-181">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Habr_Awal" title="Habr Awal">Habr Awal</a> subclan of the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a> form the majority of the population living in both the northern and western portions of the <a href="/wiki/Maroodi_Jeex" title="Maroodi Jeex">Maroodi Jeex</a> region, including the cities and towns of northern <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabiley" title="Gabiley">Gabiley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Da%27ar_buduq" title="Da'ar buduq">Madheera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wajaale" class="mw-redirect" title="Wajaale">Wajaale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabsiyo" title="Arabsiyo">Arabsiyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulhar" title="Bulhar">Bulhar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalabaydh" title="Kalabaydh">Kalabaydh</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Habr_Awal" title="Habr Awal">Habr Awal</a> also have a strong presence in the <a href="/wiki/Sahil,_Somaliland" title="Sahil, Somaliland">Saaxil</a> region as well, principally around the city of <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a> and the town of <a href="/wiki/Sheikh,_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh, Somalia">Sheikh</a>. They also partially inhabit the city of <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a> in <a href="/wiki/Togdheer" title="Togdheer">Togdheer</a> region as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Garhajis" title="Garhajis">Garhajis</a> subclan of the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a> have a sizable presence among the population inhabiting the southern and eastern portions of <a href="/wiki/Maroodi_Jeex" title="Maroodi Jeex">Maroodi Jeex</a> region including Southern <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salahlay" title="Salahlay">Salahlay</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Garhajis" title="Garhajis">Garhajis</a> are also represented well in western <a href="/wiki/Togdheer" title="Togdheer">Togdheer</a> region, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Oodweyne" title="Oodweyne">Oodweyne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Sheikh,_Somaliland" title="Sheikh, Somaliland">Sheekh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sahil,_Somaliland" title="Sahil, Somaliland">Sahil</a> region. The <a href="/wiki/Garhajis" title="Garhajis">Garhajis</a> also have a significant presence in the western and central areas of <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a> region as well, including the regional capital <a href="/wiki/Erigavo" title="Erigavo">Erigavo</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Maydh" title="Maydh">Maydh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Habr_Je%27lo" title="Habr Je'lo">Habr Je'lo</a> subclan of the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a> have a large presence in the western and northern parts of <a href="/wiki/Sool,_Somalia" title="Sool, Somalia">Sool</a>, eastern <a href="/wiki/Togdheer" title="Togdheer">Togdheer</a> region and western <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a> as well,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Habr_Je%27lo" title="Habr Je'lo">Habr Je'lo</a> form a majority of the population living in <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a> as well as in the <a href="/wiki/Togdheer" title="Togdheer">Togdheer</a> region, western <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a>, including the towns of <a href="/wiki/Garadag" title="Garadag">Garadag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xiis" class="mw-redirect" title="Xiis">Xiis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceel_Afweyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceel Afweyn">Ceel Afweyn</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aynabo_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Aynabo District">Aynabo district</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sool,_Somalia" title="Sool, Somalia">Sool</a>. The clan also has a significant presence in the <a href="/wiki/Sahil,_Somaliland" title="Sahil, Somaliland">Sahil</a> region, particularly in the towns of <a href="/wiki/Karin,_Sahil" title="Karin, Sahil">Karin</a> and <a href="/wiki/El-Darad" title="El-Darad">El-Darad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somali_People.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Somali_People.jpg/220px-Somali_People.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Somali_People.jpg/330px-Somali_People.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Somali_People.jpg/440px-Somali_People.jpg 2x" data-file-width="574" data-file-height="415"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somali_People.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Issa man and woman in traditional attire (1844)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eastern <a href="/wiki/Sool,_Somalia" title="Sool, Somalia">Sool</a> region's residents mainly hail from the <a href="/wiki/Dhulbahante" title="Dhulbahante">Dhulbahante</a>, a subdivision of the <a href="/wiki/Harti_(Darod)" class="mw-redirect" title="Harti (Darod)">Harti</a> confederation of <a href="/wiki/Darod" title="Darod">Darod</a> sub-clans, and are concentrated at <a href="/wiki/Las_Anod" title="Las Anod">Las Anod</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> The Dhulbahante clans also settle in the <a href="/wiki/Buuhoodle_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Buuhoodle District">Buuhoodle District</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Togdheer" title="Togdheer">Togdheer</a> region,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> and the southern and eastern parts of <a href="/wiki/Erigavo_District" title="Erigavo District">Erigavo District</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-189">[189]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Warsangali" title="Warsangali">Warsangali</a>, another Harti Darod sub-clan, constitute a large number of residents in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Sanaag" title="Sanaag">Sanaag</a>, and their population is mainly concentrated around <a href="/wiki/Las_Khorey" title="Las Khorey">Las Qorey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-189">[189]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="Languages of Somaliland">Languages of Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Many people in Somaliland speak two of the three official languages: <a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, although the rate of bilingualism is lower in rural areas. Article 6 of the Constitution of 2001 designates the official language of Somaliland to be Somali,<sup id="cite_ref-const_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-const-16">[16]</a></sup> though Arabic is a mandatory subject in school and is used in <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> around the region and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is spoken and taught in schools. English was proclaimed an official language later, outside the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Somali language is the mother tongue of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">Somali people</a>, the nation's most populous ethnic group. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Afro-Asiatic_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Asiatic languages">Afro-Asiatic</a> language family, and its nearest relatives are the <a href="/wiki/Oromo_language" title="Oromo language">Oromo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saho_language" title="Saho language">Saho</a> languages.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Somali is the best documented of the Cushitic languages,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> with academic studies of it dating from before 1900. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Northern_Somali" title="Northern Somali">Northern Somali</a> is the main dialect spoken in the country, in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Benadiri_Somali" title="Benadiri Somali">Benadiri Somali</a> which is the main dialect spoken in Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="Islam in Somaliland">Islam in Somaliland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Somaliland" title="Christianity in Somaliland">Christianity in Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG/170px-Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG/255px-Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG/340px-Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="4752"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Korantafel_im_%C3%9Cberseemuseum_03.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional Somali <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur'an">Qur'anic</a> tablet.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With few exceptions, Somalis in Somaliland and elsewhere are <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>, the majority belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi'i">Shafi'i</a> school of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_jurisprudence" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic jurisprudence">Islamic jurisprudence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mohamed_Diriye_Abdullahi_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mohamed_Diriye_Abdullahi-194">[194]</a></sup> As with southern Somali coastal towns such as <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merca" title="Merca">Merca</a>, there is also a presence of <a href="/wiki/Sufi_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi Islam">Sufism</a>, Islamic mysticism; particularly the Arab Rifa'iya <a href="/wiki/Tariqa" title="Tariqa">tariiqa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewissaisom_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewissaisom-195">[195]</a></sup> Through the influence of the diaspora from Yemen and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf states</a>, stricter <a href="/wiki/Wahhabism" title="Wahhabism">Wahhabism</a> also has a noticeable presence.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Though traces of pre-Islamic traditional religion exist in Somaliland, Islam is dominant to the Somali sense of national identity. Many of the Somali social norms come from their religion. For example, most Somali women wear a <a href="/wiki/Hijab" title="Hijab">hijab</a> when they are in public. In addition, religious Somalis abstain from <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a>, and also try to avoid receiving or paying any form of interest (<a href="/wiki/Usury" title="Usury">usury</a>). Muslims generally congregate on Friday afternoons for a sermon and group prayer.<sup id="cite_ref-somarel_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somarel-197">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Somaliland" title="Constitution of Somaliland">Constitution of Somaliland</a>, Islam is the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, and no laws may violate the principles of <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a>. The promotion of any religion other than Islam is illegal, and the state promotes Islamic tenets and discourages behaviour contrary to "Islamic morals".<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somaliland has very few <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>. In 1913, during the early part of the colonial era, there were virtually no Christians in the Somali territories, with about 100–200 followers coming from the schools and orphanages of the handful of <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> missions in the British Somaliland protectorate.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> The small number of Christians in the region today mostly come from similar Catholic institutions in <a href="/wiki/Aden" title="Aden">Aden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somaliland falls within the Episcopal Area of the Horn of Africa as part of Somalia, under the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Diocese_of_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican Diocese of Egypt">Anglican Diocese of Egypt</a>. However, there are no current congregations in the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Mogadiscio" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Mogadiscio">Roman Catholic Diocese of Mogadiscio</a> is designated to serve the area as part of Somalia. However, since 1990 there has been no Bishop of Mogadishu, and the Bishop of Djibouti acts as Apostolic Administrator.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Adventist_Mission" title="Adventist Mission">Adventist Mission</a> also indicates that there are no Adventist members.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare in Somaliland">Healthcare in Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg/220px-Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg/330px-Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg/440px-Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Edna_Adan_Hospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Edna_Adan_Maternity_Hospital" title="Edna Adan Maternity Hospital">Edna Adan Maternity Hospital</a> in Hargeisa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>While 40.5% of households in Somaliland have access to improved water sources, almost a third of households lie at least an hour away from their primary source of drinking water. 1 in 11 children die before their first birthday, and 1 in 9 die before their fifth birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UNICEF multiple indicator cluster survey (MICS) in 2006 found that 94.8% of women in Somaliland had undergone some form of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-205">[205]</a></sup> in 2018 the Somaliland government issued a fatwa condemning the two most severe forms of FGM, but no laws are present to punish those responsible for the practice.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-205">[205]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Somaliland" title="Sports in Somaliland">Sports in Somaliland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hargeisa_(28986744304).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Hargeisa_%2828986744304%29.jpg/220px-Hargeisa_%2828986744304%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Hargeisa_%2828986744304%29.jpg/330px-Hargeisa_%2828986744304%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Hargeisa_%2828986744304%29.jpg/440px-Hargeisa_%2828986744304%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3142" data-file-height="2356"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hargeisa_(28986744304).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>People in <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somaliland has a population of about 3.5 million people. As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somaliland&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the largest clan family in Somaliland is the <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a>, making up 80% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> The populations of five major cities in Somaliland – <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burao" title="Burao">Burao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erigavo" title="Erigavo">Erigavo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabiley" title="Gabiley">Gabiley</a> – are predominantly Isaaq.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Of the minority clans, the <a href="/wiki/Gadabuursi" title="Gadabuursi">Gadabuursi</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dir_clan" class="mw-redirect" title="Dir clan">Dir clan</a> comes second by population, and thirdly the <a href="/wiki/Harti" title="Harti">Harti</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Darod" title="Darod">Darod</a> clan.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Clan" title="Clan">clan</a> groupings of the Somali people are important <a href="/wiki/Social_unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Social unit">social units</a>, and have a central role in Somali culture and politics. Clans are <a href="/wiki/Patrilineality" title="Patrilineality">patrilineal</a> and are often divided into sub-clans, sometimes with many sub-divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somali society is traditionally ethnically <a href="/wiki/Endogamy" title="Endogamy">endogamous</a>. To extend ties of alliance, marriage is often to another <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Somalis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Somalis">ethnic Somali</a> from a different clan. Thus, for example, a recent study observed that in 89 marriages contracted by men of the <a href="/wiki/Dhulbahante" title="Dhulbahante">Dhulbahante</a> clan, 55 (62%) were with women of Dhulbahante sub-clans other than those of their husbands; 30 (33.7%) were with women of surrounding clans of other clan families (<a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a>, 28; <a href="/wiki/Hawiye" title="Hawiye">Hawiye</a>, 3); and 3 (4.3%) were with women of other clans of the <a href="/wiki/Darod" title="Darod">Darod</a> clan family (<a href="/wiki/Majerteen" class="mw-redirect" title="Majerteen">Majerteen</a> 2, <a href="/wiki/Ogaden_(clan)" title="Ogaden (clan)">Ogaden</a> 1).<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somaliland&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2021</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Canjeelo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Canjeelo.jpg/220px-Canjeelo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Canjeelo.jpg/330px-Canjeelo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Canjeelo.jpg/440px-Canjeelo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="451"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Canjeelo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Somali <a href="/wiki/Lahoh" title="Lahoh">lahoh</a> (<i>canjeero</i>).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>It is considered polite to leave a little bit of food on the plate after finishing a meal at another's home. This tells the host that one has been given enough food. If plates are picked clean it is an indication that guests are still hungry. Most Somalis do not take this rule so seriously, but it is certainly not impolite to leave a few bits of food on one's plate. Somali breakfast typically includes a flatbread called <a href="/wiki/Lahoh" title="Lahoh">lahoh</a> (<a href="/wiki/Injera" title="Injera">injera</a>), as well as <a href="/wiki/Liver_(food)" title="Liver (food)">liver</a>, toast, harakoo, cereal, and <a href="/wiki/Porridge" title="Porridge">porridge</a> made of <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cornmeal" title="Cornmeal">cornmeal</a>. Lunch can be a mixture of rice or pasta with meat and sauce. </p>
      <p>Also consumed during lunchtime is a traditional soup referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">maraq</a></i>, which is also part of <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemeni</a> cuisine. Maraq is made of vegetables, meat and beans and is usually eaten with flatbread or <a href="/wiki/Pita" title="Pita">pita</a> bread. Later in the day, a lighter meal is served that includes <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ful_medames" title="Ful medames">ful medames</a>, muffo (patties made of oats or corn), or a salad with more lahoh/<a href="/wiki/Injera" title="Injera">injera</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:137px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hadrawi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hadrawi.jpg/135px-Hadrawi.jpg" decoding="async" width="135" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hadrawi.jpg/203px-Hadrawi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hadrawi.jpg/270px-Hadrawi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hadrawi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hadrawi" title="Hadrawi">Hadrawi</a>, a prominent Somali poet and <a href="/wiki/Songwriter" title="Songwriter">songwriter</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a> have been described as the twin pillars of Somali culture. Somali poetry is mainly oral, with both male and female poets. They use things that are common in the Somali language as metaphors. Almost all Somalis are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslims</a> and Islam is vitally important to the Somali sense of <a href="/wiki/National_identity" title="National identity">national identity</a>. Most Somalis do not belong to a specific <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> or sect and can pray in any mosque they find.<sup id="cite_ref-somarel_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somarel-197">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Celebrations come in the form of religious festivities. Two of the most important are <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Adha" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Adha">Eid ul-Adha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid ul-Fitr</a>, which marks the end of the fasting month. Families get dressed up to visit one another, and money is donated to the poor. Other holidays include 26 June and 18 May, which celebrate British Somaliland's independence and the Somaliland region's establishment, respectively; the latter, however, is not recognised by the international community.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Henna_for_hair.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Henna_for_hair.jpg/220px-Henna_for_hair.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Henna_for_hair.jpg/330px-Henna_for_hair.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Henna_for_hair.jpg/440px-Henna_for_hair.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Henna_for_hair.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Henna" title="Henna">Henna</a> powder is mixed with water and then applied on the hair.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> culture, where one's possessions are frequently moved, there is little reason for the <a href="/wiki/Plastic_arts" title="Plastic arts">plastic arts</a> to be highly developed. Somalis embellish and decorate their woven and wooden milk jugs (<i>haamo</i>; the most decorative jugs are made in <a href="/wiki/Ceerigaabo" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceerigaabo">Ceerigaabo</a>) as well as wooden headrests.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Traditional dance is also important, though mainly as a form of courtship among young people. One such dance known as <i>Ciyaar Soomaali</i> is a local favourite.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An important form of art in Somali culture is <a href="/wiki/Henna" title="Henna">henna</a> art. The custom of applying henna dates back to antiquity. During special occasions, a Somali woman's hands and feet are expected to be covered in decorative <a href="/wiki/Mendhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mendhi">mendhi</a>. Girls and women usually apply or decorate their hands and feet in henna on festive celebrations like <a href="/wiki/Muslim_holidays" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim holidays">Eid</a> or weddings. The henna designs vary from very simple to highly intricate. Somali designs vary, with some more modern and simple while others are traditional and intricate. Traditionally, only women apply it as <a href="/wiki/Body_art" title="Body art">body art</a>, as it is considered a feminine custom. Henna is not only applied on the hands and feet but is also used as a <a href="/wiki/Dye" title="Dye">dye</a>. Somali men and women alike use henna as a dye to change their hair colour. Women are free to apply henna on their hair as most of the time they are wearing a <a href="/wiki/Hijab" title="Hijab">hijab</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (May 2021)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>

        <li id="cite_note-ILGA-113"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ILGA_113-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://old.ilga.org/Statehomophobia/ILGA_SSHR_2014_Eng.pdf">STATE-SPONSORED HOMOPHOBIA </a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20161020202330/http://old.ilga.org/Statehomophobia/ILGA_SSHR_2014_Eng.pdf">Archived</a> 20 October 2016 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://freedomhouse.org/report/freedom-world/2017/somaliland">"Somaliland * – Country report – Freedom in the World – 2017"</a>. <i>freedomhouse.org</i>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=freedomhouse.org&amp;rft.atitle=Somaliland+%2A+%E2%80%93+Country+report+%E2%80%93+Freedom+in+the+World+%E2%80%93+2017&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Ffreedomhouse.org%2Freport%2Ffreedom-world%2F2017%2Fsomaliland&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASomaliland" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-Kaplan248252-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Kaplan248252_115-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFKaplan2008" class="citation journal cs1">Kaplan, Seth (July 2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sethkaplan.org/doc/JOD,%20Democratization%20in%20Africa%20chapter%203.10.pdf">"The Remarkable Story of Somaliland"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Journal of Democracy</i>. <b>19</b>: 248 &amp; 252<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 August</span> 2017</span>. <q>The Republic of Somaliland, the secessionist northwestern slice of Somalia that declared independence in 1991, has a far better democratic track record than any of its neighbors despite—or, perhaps, because of—a dearth of assistance from the international community.[...] Whereas attempts to build stable state structures in Mogadishu have mostly been top-down, with outsiders in the lead, Somaliland has constructed a functioning government from the bottom up, on its own, with little outside assistance.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Democracy&amp;rft.atitle=The+Remarkable+Story+of+Somaliland&amp;rft.volume=19&amp;rft.pages=248+%26+252&amp;rft.date=2008-07&amp;rft.aulast=Kaplan&amp;rft.aufirst=Seth&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.sethkaplan.org%2Fdoc%2FJOD%2C%2520Democratization%2520in%2520Africa%2520chapter%25203.10.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASomaliland" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-Kaplan248249253-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Kaplan248249253_116-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFKaplan2008" class="citation journal cs1">Kaplan, Seth (July 2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sethkaplan.org/doc/JOD,%20Democratization%20in%20Africa%20chapter%203.10.pdf">"The Remarkable Story of Somaliland"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Journal of Democracy</i>. <b>19</b>: 248–249 &amp; 253<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 August</span> 2017</span>. <q>Abutting the Gulf of Aden just south of the Red Sea, across the water from Yemen and Saudi Arabia, and bordered by Ethiopia and the rest of Somalia, this strategically important territory is not even recognized by the international community but undoubtedly has the most democratic political system in the entire Horn of Africa. In contrast to the chaos and extremist threats that continue to plague much of the rest of Somalia—and unlike the authoritarian regimes that throng its neighborhood—Somaliland has held three consecutive competitive elections since its constitutional referendum in 2001, has a parliament controlled by opposition parties, and boasts a vibrant economy dominated by the private sector. Somaliland has achieved these successes by constructing a set of governing bodies rooted in traditional Somali concepts of governance by consultation and consent. In contrast to most postcolonial states in Africa and the Middle East, Somaliland has had a chance to administer itself using customary norms, values, and relationships. In fact, its integration of traditional ways of governance within a modern state apparatus has helped it to achieve greater cohesion and legitimacy and— not coincidentally—create greater room for competitive elections and public criticism than exists in most similarly endowed territories.[...] Somaliland has profited from a unity conferred by its comparatively homogeneous population, modest disparities in personal wealth, widespread fear of the south, and a lack of outside interference that might have undermined the accountability that has been forced on its leaders. This cohesiveness—which makes Somaliland sharply distinct from both Somalia and most other African states—has combined with the enduring strength of traditional institutions of self-governance to mold a unique form of democracy.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Democracy&amp;rft.atitle=The+Remarkable+Story+of+Somaliland&amp;rft.volume=19&amp;rft.pages=248-249+%26+253&amp;rft.date=2008-07&amp;rft.aulast=Kaplan&amp;rft.aufirst=Seth&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.sethkaplan.org%2Fdoc%2FJOD%2C%2520Democratization%2520in%2520Africa%2520chapter%25203.10.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASomaliland" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
